includes BMSP only 
Source: City of San Mateo Multi-Family Housing Applications from 2019 - present 
 
From Table 3 above, it was determined that sites on the inventory () that had either a commercial, 
downtown, executive office, or transit-oriented development zone could be developed to 90% of capacity. 
Meanwhile, sites that were zoned for multi-family or other residential zoning could be developed to 75% 
of capacity. These factors were multiplied by site acreage and maximum units per acre allowed by zoning 
to create the realistic capacity assumptions in the Sites Inventory table.  
 
4.8.1 General Plan Adoption and Revised Development Capacities 
In the original 2023-2031 Housing Element, it was determined that projects in commercial, downtown, 
executive office, or transit-oriented development zones could be developed at 90% of capacity, and for 
all other multifamily residential districts, 75% of capacity. This was determined with a maximum density 
of 50 du/ac and a five-story height limit. With the adoption of General Plan 2040 and passage of 
Measure T, many sites have an increased allowed density as compared to the site’s zoning district with 
new land use designations and a site’s development potential is not bound to the zoning district 
designation, but rather the General Plan 2040 land use designation.   
 
Since the adoption of Measure T in November 2024, the City has received 11 preliminary/formal 
applications (Table 1a) - not including the Hillsdale Mall redevelopment - that largely take advantage of 
the increased densities of up to 130 du/ac and up to eight-story height limits.  Most of the sites are 
being proposed well above the General Plan densities. Of the 11 projects, seven are on sites between a 
half-acre and less than 10 acres and have capacities that are 118% to 200% of the base density (see 
Table 4a). Although there are a limited number of development projects, there does not seem to be any 
capacity trends between mixed-use or residential designations nor allowed densities. The other four 
projects are on sites that are under a half-acre or more than 10 acres. These projects, which are 
noticeable outliers, have lower capacities that range from 35% to 85% of base density. Altogether, new 
development projects are building at an average of 122% of base density.

--- page 213 ---
C I T Y  O F  S A N  M A T E O  2 0 3 1  H O U S I N G  E L E M E N T  
Page H-C-67 
Table 4a: Preliminary and Formal Applications by Site Size and Realistic Capacity 
Site Sizes 
Avg. % Exceeding Realistic Capacity 
Small (<0.5 acres) 
65% 
Medium (>0.5 acres) 
183% 
Large (>1 acres) 
141% 
>10 Acres 
47% 
 
Based on all the current trend of projects and particularly projects on sites between 0.5 acre and 10 
acres the City revised its determination that a realistic capacity of 90% of the allowed density for all 
sites, regardless of General Plan land use designation, is feasible.  
 
Table 2, along with the full body of the Housing Element, demonstrates that the City of San Mateo has 
developed a Sites Inventory with a sufficient number of housing opportunity sites with appropriate 
densities, defensible realistic capacity estimates and near-term development feasibility to meet and 
exceed the City’s RHNA of 7,015 units.

San Mateo Housing Element (2023-2031)
• Adopted on May 20, 2024, certified by the State 
Housing and Community Development Department 
(HCD) on July 23, 2024
• Five goals to support compliance with state law and to 
achieve the City’s RHNA (7,015 units) – Supporting 
Production, Preservation, Protection, Promotion, and 
Affirmatively Furthering Fair Housing
• Includes 53 policies with 150 implementation actions
• Numerous Housing Element policies and programs that 
require Zoning Code Amendments and policy 
amendments

November 2023 - Amended the Zoning Code to allow residential projects with up to 25 
units to be approved administratively. (Policy H1.6)
November 2023 - Adopted Objective Design Standards for multi-family residential 
projects and mixed-use projects with a residential component. (Policy H1.8)
July 2024 – Housing “By-Right” designation for housing sites reused from prior Housing 
Elements for housing projects. Minimum 20% affordable units and zoning must be at 
least 30 units/acre (Policy H1.10)

Actions/Programs (variety) and State Law Compliance; increased Zoning Administrator 
threshold for residential project approval to 99 units; added sections for General Plan and 
Measure T consistency (Variety of Policies)

City Hall
330 W. 20th Avenue
San Mateo CA 94403
www.cityofsanmateo.org
Agenda Number:  3
Section Name: PUBLIC HEARING
File ID: 26-10822
TO:
Planning Commission
FROM:
Zachary Dahl, Director 
PREPARED BY:
Community Development Department
MEETING DATE:
January 27, 2025 
SUBJECT:
3399 CSM Drive - Special Use Permit (SUP) for a new Child Care Center in an Existing Church (PA-2025-053) 
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution to approve a Special Use Permit (SUP) to allow for a new child care center use in an existing church 
building, subject to findings and conditions of approval, and find it exempt from CEQA pursuant to Section 15301 (Existing 
Facilities).
BACKGROUND:
The Western Hills Church, located at 3399 CSM Drive, is a religious institution within a residential zoning district (R1-A).  The 
church was originally founded in 1947 as the “Central Baptist Church of San Mateo,” where members would meet in 
Downtown San Mateo. In 1962, the church purchased the property at 3399 CSM and renamed itself as “The First Southern 
Baptist Church.” In 1978, the Planning Commission approved a Special Use Permit (SUP) (under Planning Application PA-
1978-005) for the establishment of the existing church. PA-1978-005 included a Site Development Permit for grading and a 
Site Plan and Architectural Review (SPAR) for construction of the church campus. At that time, the facility included a 
sanctuary, an office, and classrooms. Since then, the church has renamed itself as “The Western Hills Church” and has 
continued to operate as permitted in 1978. 
In 2017, the Church allowed a tenant to run an after-school program with approximately 20 children, but did not have a City 
approved Special Use Permit (SUP). The after-school program concluded in 2025. A new tenant subsequently proposed to 
establish a licensed child care program serving up to 60 children. During the state licensing process, the operator was 
required to provide documentation of City approval prior to commencing operations, which prompted the submission of 
the current SUP application. The SUP will also require tenant improvements to comply with the current building code 
requirements for the occupancy and number of children proposed for the child care center.  The church is requesting 
approval of a SUP to use approximately 2,976 square feet of existing interior space for a child care facility serving up to 60 
children up to four years in age, with five staff members. As part of this request, the church also seeks to update the 
Conditions of Approval associated with its previously approved SUP (PA-1978-005). The current planning application 
proposes to update the Conditions of Approval from the previous SUP and to use a portion of the existing church space for 
the proposed child care use. 
SITE DESCRIPTION:
The two-acre site (87,405 square feet) is developed with a 22,420 square-foot church facility that includes a sanctuary, 
classrooms, kitchens, dressing rooms, music rooms, storage, and bathrooms, that was approved and constructed in 1978.  
The property is accessed off CSM Drive and is adjacent to the College of San Mateo Parking lot at 3403 CSM Drive.  
Surrounding uses include two-family residential developments to the north and east, the San Mateo Highlands 
(Unincorporated) to the south, and multi-family apartments to the west. The site has a General Plan land use designation of 
Quasi-Public and is zoned R1-A (One Family Dwellings).  A location map showing the project and its vicinity is included as

--- page 238 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
Attachment 2.
PROJECT DESCRIPTION:
The applicant proposes to convert portions of the existing church, including five classrooms, and a reception room 
(previously approved as a Sunday School for the church), which is approximately 2,976 square feet of existing building area 
into a child care center for up to 60 preschool-aged children (infants to four years old) and five staff members. The child care 
center is also comprised of ancillary and support spaces including a reception area. Following approval of the SUP, the 
applicant will need to apply for tenant improvements to update the facility to comply with current Building and Fire Codes 
for the proposed occupancy type and number of allowed children. The child care program would also use an existing outdoor 
play area on the north side of the building that is surrounded by a three-foot high metal fence. The site is already improved 
with a parking lot that has 103 parking spaces and sufficient loading/unloading space for the child care use. The child care 
center will operate weekdays (Monday to Friday) from 8:00 am to 6:00 pm. A written description from the applicant with 
additional information about the proposed use is included as Attachment 3. The project plans are included as Attachment 
4, which also includes a site circulation plan used for drop-off and pick-up.
APPLICABLE CODE AND POLICY REVIEW:
State Laws
The Department of Social Services Community Care Licensing Division regulates and licenses child care centers and small 
and large family child care homes. There are two primary types of child care: Family Child Care Homes and Child Care Centers. 
Child Care Center means any child care facility of any capacity, other than a family child care home, in which less than 24-
hour per day nonmedical care and supervision are provided to children in a group setting (California Code of Regulations, 
Title 22, Division 12, Section 101152(a)(7)). This definition is used for state licensing purposes under the Community Care 
Licensing Act. Before receiving a state license, applicants must obtain a business license and approval from the City of San 
Mateo. Previously, the applicant and State unknowingly allowed tenants to operate a child care center without City approval 
since 2017. While trying to obtain their State license for a new expanded child care center operation, the State requested 
proof of approval from the City, which led to the application for this SUP. 
General Plan and Zoning Code
The General Plan land use designation for the project site is Quasi-Public, which is intended for uses such as schools and 
faith-based institutions. The zoning designation for the project site is R1-A, which allows for child care centers within a public 
or quasi-public structure, such as a church, school, temple, or similar facility, with a SUP, pursuant to SMMC Section 
27.18.030(h). Residential uses allow family day cares (referred to as Family Care Homes by the state) as a by-right use (SMMC 
27.18.020(f)(3), while child care centers (referred to as day care centers in the Zoning Code) require a special use permit 
(SMMC 27.18.030(h)). SMMC 27.85.020 regulates child care center development standards and includes conditions of use. 
The proposed project provides a neighborhood-serving use – child care center within a residential zoning district – which is 
supported by General Plan Policies LU 3.5 and PSF 6.5 and allowed in the zoning code with a Special Use Permit. The proposed 
child care center meets the Zoning Code’s child care standards and includes the required conditions of use outlined in SMMC 
27.85.020. A full list of applicable General Plan policies, zoning code requirements, and a discussion of the project’s 
conformance to them is included in the Resolution in Attachment 1. 
Special Use Permit (SUP)
The applicant proposes to establish a child care center within a religious facility in the One Family Dwelling (R1-A) zoning 
district and to update the existing church’s conditions of approval. Pursuant to SMMC Section 27.18.030(d), churches are 
allowed with approval of a Special Use Permit (SUP), and SMMC Section 27.18.030(h) allows for child care centers in quasi-
public structures with approval of a Special Use Permit (SUP). Aside from the unpermitted child care center that operated 
since 2017, the project is consistent with the previously approved church entitlements under PA-1978-005, as it utilizes the 
existing building footprint, parking, and site layout, with no exterior modifications. The proposed child care center was 
reviewed to ensure compliance with the Zoning Code standards in SMMC 27.85.020. The conditions include a detailed 
description of allowed uses and operations for the existing church and proposed child care center, and for tenant 
improvements to ensure compliance with current building, fire, security, and zoning standards.  Findings and the Conditions 
of Approval are included in Attachment 1.

--- page 239 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
Parking and Circulation Analysis
The proposed project requires 11 parking spaces and six loading spaces for the child care center (the project can reduce the 
loading space requirement to five if staff members are assisting students) and the church use requires 44 parking spaces 
with no loading requirement, pursuant to SMMC Section 27.64.160. The existing site has 103 parking spaces on-site and five 
proposed loading/unloading spaces (with assistance from staff) around the perimeter of the building and a circular drive 
aisle to access the parking area. With the addition of the child care program, the site remains in compliance with the parking 
requirements. Drop-off and pick-up will occur within the existing church parking lot, utilizing the circular drive aisle with 
designated loading/unloading areas. Parents will be able to enter the site from CSM Drive and drive counterclockwise around 
the parking lot area. Drop-off operations will be managed through staggered drop-off periods and staff-assisted unloading. 
This will help prevent disruptions and spillage to the local traffic network. See Sheet 2 of the project plans (Attachment 4) 
for the site access and circulation plan.
A Parking and Traffic Management Plan was prepared for the project to coordinate traffic circulation and drop-off and pick-
up operations (Attachment 5). This plan identifies designated drop-off and pick-up locations, outlines procedures, and 
establishes a monitoring program to ensure safe and efficient circulation.  The school will provide dedicated staff to monitor 
and direct traffic during drop-off and pick-up periods in accordance with the Parking and Traffic Management Plan.  Per 
Condition 22, if any queuing issues arise, the applicant shall implement appropriate operational measures to minimize or 
eliminate the problem. These operational adjustments may include, but are not limited to, reducing class sizes, decreasing 
the number of classes, securing additional loading zones, conducting a queuing analysis, or any other measures deemed 
appropriate by the Community Development Director or his/her designee.
Traffic Impact Analysis - Vehicle Miles Traveled and Local Transportation Analysis
The City adopted Traffic Impact Analysis (TIA) Guidelines to evaluate transportation related impacts from proposed projects. 
The guidelines discuss two types of analyses to be conducted including vehicle miles traveled (VMT) analysis that addresses 
transportation impacts under the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) and local transportation analysis (LTA) that 
addresses traffic congestion and traffic operations under General Plan policies. 
The City established VMT screening thresholds in the Traffic Impact Analysis Guidelines.  According to the guidelines, local-
serving retail and public service uses of 50,000 square feet or less are generally presumed to have a less-than-significant 
VMT impact. The guidelines allow the determination of a local-serving use based on a project’s location, characteristics, 
surrounding area, and the types of goods or services provided. The use, which encompasses approximately 2,976 square 
feet, provides a service to local residents living in the surrounding neighborhoods or employees working in the surrounding 
area that typically redistribute existing trips rather than generate new ones. Therefore, the facility qualifies as a local-serving 
use under 50,000 square feet and is exempt from VMT analysis.
With regards to the local transportation analysis, consistent with General Plan Circulation Element Policy C 6.3, the TIA 
guidelines states that the City may require site specific traffic studies for development projects where there may be a 
substantial adverse condition or effect on the local street system. Public Works staff reviewed the proposed project, the 
parking and circulation plan, the surrounding intersections, and determined that the project does not adversely affect the 
local circulation system because there is sufficient on-site loading and unloading areas and traffic circulates through the 
parking lot before returning to the street. Also, the project is estimated to generate 47 peak hour AM and PM trips according 
to the Institute for Transportation Engineers (ITE) trip generation rate estimates. Public Works evaluated the estimated trip 
generation and given the limited number of peak-hour trips and the fact that all circulation is accommodated on site, the 
project is not expected to materially affect nearby street and intersection operations. The closest major intersection to the 
project site is Hillsdale Blvd./Clearview Way and the added number of vehicle trips is unlikely to have a significant impact on 
the intersection since it is operating well below the acceptable level of delay.
NOTICE PROVIDED:
In accordance with Government Code Section 65091 and the City’s Municipal Code noticing requirements, this public hearing 
was noticed to the following parties more than ten days in advance of this Planning Commission meeting:

--- page 240 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
•
Property owners, residential tenants and business tenants within 1,000 feet of the project site.
•
The City’s Planning “Notify Me” email list; and
•
The interested parties list, which includes interested individuals who contacted the City and requested to be added 
to the project notification list.
PUBLIC COMMENTS:
No public comments were submitted to staff as of the publication of this agenda report.  Any additional public comments 
submitted after agenda publication will be posted to this item on the City’s Public Meeting Portal as “Post-Packet Public 
Comments.”
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
The proposed project is exempt from the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) pursuant to CEQA Guidelines Section 
15301 (Class 1 – Existing Facilities). The Class 1 exemption applies to projects involving the operation, repair, maintenance, 
or minor alteration of existing public or private structures, including interior alterations such as interior partitions, plumbing, 
and electrical conveyances, where there is negligible or no expansion of use (CEQA Guidelines §15301). The project consists 
of the interior conversion of existing space within an existing church building to accommodate a child care facility and 
updates to previously approved Conditions of Approval. No expansion of building footprint, height, or site development is 
proposed. The proposed project does not authorize any physical development, demolition, grading, or land disturbance and 
has no potential to result in a physical change to the environment. Any future physical improvements or changes in use on 
the site would remain subject to separate discretionary approvals and environmental review, as applicable. For these 
reasons, the proposed project qualifies for a categorical exemption under CEQA Guidelines Section 15301.

CITY OF SAN MATEO RESOLUTION NO. ____ (2026) 
 
A RESOLUTION OF THE PLANNING COMMISSION OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO TO APPROVE A SPECIAL 
USE PERMIT (SUP) (PA-2025-053) FOR A CHILD CARE CENTER AT AN EXISTING CHURCH AT 3399 CSM 
DRIVE (APN 041-330-020)
WHEREAS, the Western Hills Church (hereinafter referred to as the “Applicant”) submitted 
Planning Application No. PA-2025-053  on June 3, 2025,  for a Special Use Permit for a child care center 
within a quasi-public structure in a R1 Zone and to update the conditions of approval at the same location 
(collectively referred to as the “Project”) in the City of San Mateo (“City”); and
WHEREAS, the Project is consistent with the applicable policies of Strive San Mateo General Plan 
2040 and other applicable codes and policies; and
WHEREAS, the General Plan’s Public Services Facilities Element has a goal to “foster the healthy 
development and education of children of all abilities, incomes, and backgrounds,” and a specific policy 
that encourages child care centers in residential neighborhoods where they meet the City standards 
(Policy PSF 6.5); and
WHEREAS, the proposed Special Use Permit includes updating the Conditions of Approval 
originally adopted under Planning Application PA-1978-005, and all prior conditions shall remain in effect 
except where modified by this approval, consistent with the Planning Commission’s authority under 
SMMC Chapter 27.74 to impose and revise conditions as necessary to ensure compliance with current 
standards; and
WHEREAS, San Mateo Municipal Code Section 27.18.030(h) permits child care centers within a 
public or quasi-public structure such as a church, school, temple, or similar facility in R1 zoning districts 
with a Special Use Permit; and
WHEREAS, pursuant to Government Code Section 65901 and San Mateo Municipal Code Section 
27.06.040, the Planning Commission is authorized to approve or deny Special Use Permits and is the final 
decision-making body for this project; and
WHEREAS, in accordance with Government Code Sections 65090 and 65091, notice of the public 
hearing was mailed to all property owners, tenants, and businesses within one thousand (1,000) feet at 
least ten (10) days prior to the hearing, consistent with San Mateo Municipal Code Section 27.08.050; and
WHEREAS, the proposed project involves the interior conversion of existing space within an 
existing church building with no expansion of building footprint, height, or site development, and pursuant 
to the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) Guidelines Section 15301 (Class 1 – Existing Facilities), 
such minor alterations to existing facilities are categorically exempt from CEQA; and
WHEREAS, on January 27, 2026, the Planning Commission held a duly noticed public hearing, at 
which time the Commission received and considered written and oral evidence, and by a vote of 
_________ approved the Special Use Permit subject to the listed Findings for Approval and Conditions of 
Approval for Planning Application No. PA-2025-053.

--- page 242 ---
PA-2025-053, 3399 CSM DR, SUP
As approved on January 27, 2026
Page 2 of 12
NOW, THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, THAT THE PLANNING COMMISSION OF THE CITY OF SAN 
MATEO, CALIFORNIA HEREBY finds and determines that, based on substantial evidence in the record:
1.
The project will not have a significant effect on the environment and is therefore categorically 
exempt from the provisions of the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) pursuant to CEQA 
Guidelines Section 15301 (Class 1 – Existing Facilities). The project consists of the interior 
conversion of an existing classroom to a child care facility with no expansion of building footprint, 
height, or overall site development. Therefore, the project involves only minor alterations to an 
existing structure to conform with current building code and qualifies for the Class 1 categorical 
exemption.
2.
This Special Use Permit (PA-2025-053) updates the Conditions of Approval originally established 
under PA-1978-005. All prior conditions remain in effect except where modified by this approval, 
consistent with the Planning Commission’s authority under SMMC Chapter 27.74 to impose and 
revise conditions as necessary to ensure compliance with current standards and the purposes of 
the zoning code.
3.
The Planning Commission approves the project based on findings and subject to the conditions of 
approval attached hereto as Exhibit A. The project updates the existing church’s Conditions of 
Approval and approves a child care use, which is expressly supported and encouraged within the 
Quasi-Public General Plan Land Use designation. This land use category accommodates facilities 
owned and/or operated by quasi-public or community-serving organizations, including schools 
and faith-based institutions, and the proposed project aligns with and advances these intended 
purposes. Additionally, the proposed child care facility complies with all applicable Municipal 
Code standards for child care uses (SMMC 27.85), and the church will continue to operate in 
compliance with the conditions associated with the previously approved Special Use Permit (PA-
1978-005), as updated herein.
General Plan Conformance
4.
The project conforms to the following Land Use Policies and Community Design and Historic 
Resources Policies of the City’s General Plan 2040.  
a
Policy LU 3.5 Support Service Uses. Encourage businesses that provide a variety of 
services, such as restaurants, child care facilities, medical clinics, gyms, pharmacies, 
hardware stores, and grocery stores in locations that serve residential neighborhoods and 
commercial/office uses. Prioritize the development of these services in equity priority 
communities in the city.  
b
Policy LU 11.1 Economic Development. Prioritize the retention and expansion of existing 
businesses and attract new businesses that strengthen and diversify the City’s economic 
base.

--- page 243 ---
PA-2025-053, 3399 CSM DR, SUP
As approved on January 27, 2026
Page 3 of 12
The proposed project is consistent with the above Land Use Element policies in that it supports 
an existing San Mateo institution, the Western Hills Church, and maintains an essential 
community service by providing a child care facility in a location that serves residential 
neighborhoods. The proposed revisions to the previously approved entitlement (PA-1978-005) 
maintain the specific tailored development standards while updating the previous conditions and 
limitations on operations. Furthermore, approval of the child care supports the City’s goal of 
retaining and strengthening existing services that provide essential neighborhood services. 
5.
The Project conforms to applicable policies of the General Plan 2040 Circulation Element. 
a.
Policy C 6.3 Local Transportation Analysis. Require site-specific transportation impact 
analysis following the City’s adopted Transportation Impact Analysis (TIA) Policy for 
development projects where there may be an adverse condition or effect on the roadway 
system.
b.
Policy C 6.4 Operations Analysis for Development Projects. Require new development to 
determine the need for new or modified circulation improvements, operations, or 
alignments where developments identify operational deficiencies that were not 
previously identified in a transportation impact fee study. Require development 
applicants to prepare an analysis to determine the need for modifications, such as 
signalization, turn restrictions, roundabouts, etc. Require applicants to fund identified off-
site improvements if warranted, as determined by the legally appropriate transportation 
analysis, and as approved by City staff.  
c.
Policy C 7.2 Shared Parking. Encourage new and existing developments, especially those 
in mixed-use districts, to share parking between uses to maximize the existing parking 
supply, minimize the amount of new parking construction, and encourage “park once” 
behavior in commercial areas.
The proposed project is consistent with the above Circulation Elements because it incorporates 
appropriate operational measures, including a Parking and Traffic Plan that ensures safe and 
efficient site access, on-site circulation, and managed drop-off/pick-up procedures to prevent 
queuing or delays from spilling onto the public street. The project also provides more on-site 
parking spaces than required for both the church and the child care uses and includes adequate 
loading areas fully contained on the property, thereby minimizing the need for additional parking 
construction and supporting efficient shared use of existing parking facilities.  
6.
The Project conforms to applicable policies of the General Plan 2040 Public Services and Facilities 
Element. 
a
Policy PSF 6.2 Child Care Needs. Support the provision of child-care programs and 
facilities to meet the needs of children of all abilities, incomes, and backgrounds through 
2040

b
Policy PSF 6.3 Provision of Child Care. Encourage public and private agencies and 
employers to provide child-care services and facilities.
c
Policy PSF 6.5 Child Care Centers in Residential and Employment Areas. Encourage 
childcare centers in residential neighborhoods where they meet City standards and at 
employment centers.
The proposed project is consistent with the above Public Services and Facilities Element 
policies in that it provides an essential childcare service within the city, helping to meet the 
community’s demand. The facility is located within a residential neighborhood, consistent 
with Policy PSF 6.5, and will operate under a Special Use Permit, which establish limitations 
on enrollment, staffing, and operations to ensure compatibility with the surrounding 
residential context. The project also supports Policies PSF 6.2 and PSF 6.3 by facilitating the 
provision of child care services through a private operator that meets City standards and 
contributes to the overall availability of child care within the community.
Special Use Permit (SUP) Findings
7.
The Special Use Permit Pursuant to SMMC 27.18.030 and 27.74.020, Special Use Permit review 
for child care centers located within a quasi-public use in an R1 District, and associated Conditions 
of Approval are approved based on the following findings. 
a
The appropriate approval body shall have the power to hear evidence that the granting 
of such permit will or will not adversely affect the general health, safety and/or welfare 
of the community, and that the use, if permitted, will not cause injury or disturbance to 
adjacent property traffic or by excessive noise, smoke, odor or noxious gas, dust, glare, 
heat or fumes, or industrial waste.
General Health
The proposed child care center use will not adversely affect the general health of the 
community, given that the use and operations of the site are required to be in compliance 
with all applicable Building Codes, Fire Codes, and the Municipal Code. 
Safety and/or welfare of the community
The proposed project will not impact matters regarding police protection, crime 
prevention, security, and welfare of the community, in that the project will comply with 
the Security, Building, and Fire regulations as conditioned. The project will increase the 
Traffic 
The project will minimize traffic disturbances to the local neighborhood through a 
required parking and traffic control plan and conditions of approval that allow the city to 
request traffic studies and/or modify operational standards as needed to reduce 
disturbances. A Parking and Traffic Plan has been incorporated to minimize potential 
neighborhood impacts, including on-site circulation measures designed to prevent 
queuing onto public streets. Additionally the eastern exit that leads to a residential street

--- page 245 ---
PA-2025-053, 3399 CSM DR, SUP
As approved on January 27, 2026
Page 5 of 12
will be temporarily blocked off during drop off and pick up times to ensure traffic 
circulates through the site onto the major street network. Should queuing or operational 
issues arise, the City may require additional operational measures as outlined in the 
Conditions of Approval. 
Excessive noise
The proposed project will follow the applicable noise regulations set forth by the City at 
all times. The outdoor play area is approximately 91 feet from the residential building to 
the west of the site, 144 feet from the single-family residences to the south, and 121 feet 
from the multifamily residences to the east. The northern side of the site abuts a vacant 
parcel. These setbacks and site conditions provide adequate separation to minimize 
potential noise impacts on surrounding properties. 
Excessive smoke, odor or noxious gas and dust
The child care center will be operated in a manner that does not generate excessive 
smoke, odor, dust or noxious gases. Any activities, equipment, or materials used on site 
will comply with applicable health, fire, and environmental regulations. The child care 
center activities include indoor class time, indoor lunch/snack time, nap time, and 
outdoor playground time. 
Glare
No new structures are proposed. Exterior lighting associated with the child care center 
will be shielded downward away from adjacent properties to prevent glare consistent 
with City lighting and security standards. 
Heat or fumes
The proposed activities from the child care center will not generate excessive heat or 
fumes. Any mechanical or HVAC equipment will be properly vented and maintained in 
accordance with applicable building and fire codes. 
Excessive industrial waste
The child care center will not generate industrial waste. Any waste associated with the 
child care center will be handled and disposed of in accordance with City requirements. 
Child Care Facilities Findings 
a
The proposed child care center complies with the applicable standards and conditions of use 
set forth in San Mateo Municipal Code Section 27.85.020, including requirements related to 
parking and loading, separation standards, hours of operation, lighting, fencing, signage, and 
compatibility with residential areas, either as proposed or as conditioned are approved based 
on the following findings.
1.
Off-street parking facilities for child care center employees and designated 
loading/unloading spaces shall meet the requirements of Chapter 27.64.

--- page 246 ---
PA-2025-053, 3399 CSM DR, SUP
As approved on January 27, 2026
Page 6 of 12
The project complies with the off-street parking and loading requirements of Chapter 
27.64 by providing the required 11 on-site parking spaces for child care employees and 5 
designated loading and unloading areas within the existing parking lot.
2.
Any new or expanding child care center shall be located at least three hundred (300) 
feet from any other child care facility requiring a special use permit, except this 
requirement would not apply to nor be affected by centers located within a public or 
quasi-public facility. The 300 feet shall be measured from property lines along the street 
frontage, on both sides of the street, and in all directions from the property, including 
around corners and across intersecting streets.
The project is a child care center located within a quasi-public facility where a special use 
permit is already required. In addition the nearest child care center is located 700 feet 
away at 3172 Clearview Way, San Mateo, CA 94402. 
3.
No outdoor play equipment shall be located in required front or street-side yards. 
The existing outdoor play equipment is not encroaching on the front or street-side yard 
setbacks, consistent with residential zone standards.
4.
Outdoor play areas shall be enclosed with a solid, six-foot high fence along property 
lines abutting residential uses. Chain-link fences with slats shall not be considered a 
solid fence.
The existing outdoor play area is enclosed by a three-foot-high fence and is located 80 
feet from the western property line and 161 feet from the eastern property line that abut 
residential zoning districts.
5.
No structural or decorative alterations are permitted that change the residential 
appearance of the building exterior. 
No structural or decorative alterations are proposed that would change the residential 
appearance of the building exterior, as all improvements are limited to interior tenant 
improvements.
6.
Nighttime security lighting shall not be directed at neighboring properties, and the light 
source shall be shielded from view off-site. 
Nighttime security lighting will be shielded and directed away from adjacent residential 
properties to prevent glare and off-site light spillover. Additionally, the property is 
surrounded by landscaping that screens the site from the adjacent residential properties.

PA-2025-053, 3399 CSM DR, SUP
As approved on January 27, 2026
Page 7 of 12
7.
Days and hours of operation shall be limited to weekdays, between the 6:30 a.m. and 
7:30 p.m. Extended days or hours may be approved by a special use permit. These hours 
may be altered only through approval of a special use permit.
The child care center will operate on weekdays within the hours of 8:00 am to 6:00 pm, 
and any extension of days or hours of operation that exceeds what is allowed in SMMC 
27.85.020(C)(5) would require approval of the Community Development Director or 
his/her designee.
8.
No signage shall be permitted for child care centers in residential districts, 
notwithstanding the provisions of Chapter 25.20
No signage is proposed for the child care center.

WRITTEN DESCRIPTION OF THE PROPOSED PROJECT 
 
Western Hills Church (WHC) is in the process of obtaining a Special Use Permit 
(SUP) from the City of San Mateo for a Preschool/Daycare program to be operated 
on its property.  Currently, there is an onsite preschool, licensed by the State for 22 
children.  The proposed new Preschool/Daycare program will be for 0–4-year-olds, 
with a total of 55-60 students.  There will be a maximum of five students for the 0–
2-year-old group, and a maximum of 55 students for the 2–4-year-old group.   
 
The proposed Preschool/Daycare facility will be on the existing first floor of the 
Western Hills Church Youth Wing.  The facility is estimated to have 2,680 square 
footages. There will be no change to the site and the existing building.   
 
Western Hills Church would also like to update the conditions of approval for the 
existing property. 
 
The detailed operations for the existing church and the proposed preschool/ 
Daycare program are as follows: 
 
Preschool/Daycare Program: 
 
• Hours of operation: from 8:00am to 6:00pm, Monday through Friday. 
 
• Number of children: a total of 55-60 students with a maximum of five 
students in the 0–2-year-old group, and a maximum of 55 students in the 2–
4-year-old group.   
 
• A total of five staff is expected.  
 
• Major activities: indoor class time (including story circle time, 
music/movement, drama play, hands on learning etc.), indoor lunch/snack 
time, indoor nap time, and outdoor playground time. 
 
• Special event: a graduation ceremony in July with an estimated attendance 
of 60. 
 
• There is no shared or separate use of indoor and outdoor spaces during the 
preschool hours of operations or the special event.

• There are 11 designated parking spaces during pick-up/drop-off time during 
pre-school hours of operation (see Site/Parking Plan).   
 
Church Office 
 
• Office hours: from 9:00 am to 12:00 pm Monday through Thursday. 
 
• There is no shared or separate use of indoor and outdoor spaces during the 
church office hours of operations. 
 
• A range of two to 6 staff/volunteers are expected. 
 
• There are 5 designated parking spaces for staff/volunteers (see Site/Parking 
Plan). 
 
Church Ministry  
 
• Weekly services: 
 
1. Early Morning Prayer: from 5:30am to 7:00am, Tuesday through 
Saturday 
2. Morning Worship Service: from 9:00am to 1:00pm, Sunday 
3. Afternoon Worship Service: from 1:30pm to 4:00pm, Sunday 
4. Evening Worship Service: from 6:00pm to 8:30pm, Saturday 
5. Worship Night: from 7:00pm to 9:00pm, Tuesday 
 
• Major Activities: sermon teaching, prayer, worship music and fellowship 
time, adult and children Sunday Schools. 
 
• A range of twenty to one hundred and fifty attendees for the weekly services. 
 
• Special events: Bible study groups, teaching classes, holiday gatherings, 
memorial services, weddings are scheduled during weekdays and Saturdays.  
 
• There is no shared or separate use of indoor and outdoor spaces during the 
regular church ministry services or special events.

1.  THE ADDRESS OF THE RESIDENCE SHALL BE PROVIDED AND PLACED IN A POSITION THAT IS READILY
VISIBLE & LEGIBLE FROM THE STREET FRONTING THE PROPERTY. NUMBERS SHALL BE A MINIMUM OF
4" HIGH WITH A MINIMUM STROKE WIDTH OF 0.5".
2.  POTABLE WATER SUPPLIES SHALL BE PROTECTED FROM CONTAMINATION CAUSED BY FIRE
PROTECTION WATER SUPPLIES. IT IS THE RESPONSIBILITY OF THE APPLICANT AND ANY
CONTRACTORS AND SUBCONTRACTORS TO CONTACT THE WATER PURVEYOR SUPPLYING THE SITE
OF SUCH PROJECT, AND TO COMPLY WITH THE REQUIREMENTS OF THAT PURVEYOR. SUCH
REQUIREMENTS SHALL BE INCORPORATED INTO THE DESIGN OF ANY WATER-BASED FIRE
PROTECTION SYSTEMS, AND/OR FIRE SUPPRESSION WATER SUPPLY SYSTEMS OR STORAGE
CONTAINERS THAT MAY BE PHYSICALLY CONNECTED IN ANY MANNER TO AN APPLIANCE CAPABLE OF
CAUSING CONTAMINATION OF THE POTABLE WATER SUPPLY OF THE PURVEYOR OF RECORD.
3.  ALL CONSTRUCTION SITES MUST COMPLY WITH APPLICABLE PROVISIONS OF THE CFC CHAPTER 33
AND OUR STANDARD DETAIL AND SPECIFICATION SI-7. 
4.  SMOKE ALARMS SHALL BE INSTALLED IN EACH SLEEPING ROOM, OUTSIDE EACH SEPARATE SLEEPING
AREA IN THE IMMEDIATE VICINITY OF THE BEDROOMS, AND ON EACH ADDITIONAL STORY OF THE
DWELLING, INCLUDING BASEMENTS AND HABITABLE ATTICS. SMOKE ALARMS SHALL BE
INTERCONNECTED, RECEIVED THEIR PRIMARY POWER FROM THE BUILDING WIRING AND SHALL BE
EQUIPPED WITH BATTERY BACKUP.
5.  AN APPROVED CARBON MONOXIDE ALARM SHALL BE INSTALLED IN DWELLING OR SLEEPING UNITS
WITHIN WHICH FUEL-BURNING APPLIANCES ARE INSTALLED AND IN SWELLING UNITS THAT HAVE AN
ATTACHED GARAGE. CARBON MONOXIDE ALARMS SHALL BE INSTALLED OUTSIDE OF EACH SEPARATE
DWELLING UNIT SLEEPING AREA IN THE IMMEDIATE VICINITY OF THE BEDROOM AND ON EVERY LEVEL
OF A DWELLING UNIT INCLUDING BASEMENTS.

GENERAL NOTES
1. CONTRACTOR SHALL COMPLY WITH ALL CALIFORNIA RESIDENTIAL CODE (CRC) 2022, CALIFORNIA
BUILDING CODE (CBC) 2022, CALIFORNIA MECHANICAL CODE (CMC) 2022, CALIFORNIA PLUMBING
CODE (CPC) 2022, CALIFORNIA FIRE CODE (CFC) 2022, CALIFORNIA ELECTRICAL CODE (CEC) 2022,
CALIFORNIA GREEN BUILDING CODE (CGBC) 2022, ENERGY EFFICIENCY STANDARDS TITLE 24.
2. SITE DRAINAGE: NO DRAINAGE ACROSS OR ONTO ADJACENT PROPERTIES OR ON SITE WATER
RETENTION. PROVIDE A MINIMUM 5% SLOPE ON PERVIOUS SURFACES AND 2% SLOPE ON
IMPERVIOUS SURFACES WITHIN 10' OF STRUCTURE.
3. FOUNDATION: SOIL UNDER SLAB AND FOOTINGS TO BE 95% COMPACTED. ALL BEARING FOOTINGS
SHALL EXTEND A MINIMUM OF 12" INTO UNDISTURBED SOIL, UNLESS OTHERWISE NOTED.
FOUNDATIONS AND HOUSE SLAB SHALL BE 2500 PSI AT 28 DAYS. FLAT WORK SHALL BE 2500 PSI AT
28 DAYS. FINISH FLOOR SLAB SHALL BE A MINIMUM OF 6" ABOVE GRADE. PROVIDE COPIES OF ANY
COMPACTION OR SOILS ANALYSIS REPORTS TO THE BUILDING DEPARTMENT PRIOR TO THE
FOUNDATION INSPECTION.
4. SILL PLATES WILL BE PRESSURE TREATED OR FOUNDATION GRADE REDWOOD.
5. ALL EXTERIOR AND INTERIOR BEARING WALLS SHALL BE 2x4 D.F. WOOD STUDS AT 16" O.C. UNLESS
OTHERWISE NOTED ON PLANS.
6. PROVIDE SOLID BLOCKING AT ALL FURRED CEILINGS AND SOFFITS AT WALLS.
7. AT ALL NON-BEARING WALLS PARALLEL TO ROOF TRUSS THAT ARE  UNBRACED FOR MORE THAN
6'-0" PROVIDE A 2x4 DIAGONAL BRACE FROM THE TOP PLATE TO THE TOP CHORD WITH A MINIMUM
OF 2-16d EACH END.
8. BOTTOM CHORD OF TRUSS TO BE BRACED AT 12' O.C. (MINIMUM).
9. ALL EXTERIOR DOOR AND WINDOW HEADERS SHALL BE 6x12 WITH  DOUBLE TOP  PLATE OVER,
UNLESS OTHERWISE NOTED.
10. POWER DRIVEN FASTENERS: ESR 2269 X-U P8 S36 AS MANUFACTURED BY "HILTI". SPACING: 18" O.C.
AT ALL BEARING WALLS, 36" O.C. AT ALL NON-BEARING WALLS.
11. EXTERIOR FINISH TO BE HORIZONTAL SIDING AT 1st FLOOR AND SHINGLE SIDING AT THE 2nd FLOOR-
SEE EXTERIOR ELEVATIONS, UNLESS OTHERWISE NOTED (U.O.N.).
12. STUCCO FINISHES AT EDGES SHALL INCLUDE THE FOLLOWING:  DRIP SCREED, SUPERIOR #1/
CASING BEAD, MILCOR #66/EXTERIOR CORNER, MILCOR #1 EXP. JOINT. INTERIOR CORNER, MILCOR
#30 EXP. JOINT.
13. ALL WINDOWS SHALL BE DUAL GLAZED WITH VINYL FRAME. SEE ELEVATIONS FOR GRIDS.
14. ALL EXTERIOR SLIDING GLASS DOORS AND WINDOWS WITH SILLS  WITHIN 18" OF THE FLOOR AND
WITHIN A 24" ARC OF EITHER VERTICAL EDGE OF AN EXTERIOR DOOR IN A CLOSED POSITION SHALL
BE TEMPERED. H.S.=HORIZONTAL SLIDER, S.H.=SINGLE HUNG, OBS.=OBSCURE, FXD.=FIXED,
TEMP.=TEMPERED, HLF. RND.=HALF ROUND.
15. SILL PLATES FOR NON-BEARING WALLS MUST BE ANCHORED TO SLAB WITH HARDENED CEMENT
NAILS.
16. EXTERIOR SILL PLATES SHALL BE CAULKED AT JOINTS WITH CONCRETE SLAB. CAULK ALL
OPENINGS IN EXTERIOR ENVELOPE,  ALL JOINTS BETWEEN DISSIMILAR MATERIALS, AND AT
JUNCTIONS OF MAJOR COMPONENTS.
17. PROVIDE ONE COAT HEAVY-BODIED ACRYLIC STAIN ON BARGE RAFTERS, FASCIA BOARDS,
EXPOSED EAVES, AND WOOD TRIM.
18. CONTRACTOR TO VERIFY ALL CONDITIONS AND DIMENSIONS IN FIELD. ANY CONFLICTS OR
DISCREPANCIES ARE TO BE BROUGHT TO THE DESIGNER'S ATTENTION PRIOR TO CONSTRUCTION.
19. BACKFLOW PREVENTER REQUIRED ON ALL HOSE BIBBS.

A4.1 PLANNING & DESIGN-SITE DEVELOPMENT
4.106.2: A PLAN IS DEVELOPED & IMPLEMENTED TO MANAGE STORM WATER DRAINAGE DURING CONSTRUCTION,
4.106.3: THE SITE SHALL BE PLANNED & DEVELOPED TO KEEP SURFACE WATER AWAY FROM BUILDINGS.
CONSTRUCTION PLANS SHALL INDICATE HOW SITE GRADING OR A DRAINAGE SYSTEMS WILL MANAGE ALL SURFACE
WATER FLOWS.
A4.2 ENERGY EFFICIENCY
4.201.1 LOW-RISE RESIDENTIAL BUILDINGS SHALL MEET OR EXCEED THE MINIMUM STANDARD DESIGN REQUIRED BY
THE CALIFORNIA ENERGY STANDARDS.
A4.3 WATER EFFICIENCY & CONSERVATION
4.303.1: INDOOR WATER USE SHALL BE REDUCED BY AT LEAST 20% USING ONE OF THE FOLLOWING METHODS:
1. WATER SAVING FIXTURES OR FLOW RESTRICTORS SHALL BE USED.
2. A 20% REDUCTION IN BASELINE WATER USE SHALL BE DEMONSTRATED.
4.303.2: WHEN USING THE CALCULATION METHODS SPECIFIED IN SECTION 4.303.1 MULTIPLE SHOWERHEADS SHALL
NOT EXCEED MAXIMUM FLOW RATES
4.303.3 PLUMBING FIXTURES (WATER CLOSETS & URINALS) & FITTINGS (FAUCETS & SHOWERHEADS) SHALL COMPLY
WITH SPECIFIED PERFORMANCE REQUIREMENTS.
OUTDOOR WATER USE:
4.304.1 OUTDOOR POTABLE WATER  USE IN LANDSCAPE AREAS.  AFTER DECEMBER  1, 2015, NEW RESIDENTIAL 
DEVELOPMENTS WITH AN AGGREGATE LANDSCAPE  AREA EQUAL TO OR GREAT THAN 500 SQUARE FEET SHALL
COMPLY 
WITH ONE OF THE FOLLOWING OPTIONS:
1. A LOCAL WATER EFFICIENT LANDSCAPE ORDINANCE OR THE CURRENT CALIFORNIA DEPARTMENT OF
WATER 
    RESOURCES' MODEL WATER EFFICIENT LANDSCAPE ORDINANCE (MWELO), WHICHEVER IS MORE
STRINGENT; OR
2. PROJECTS WITH AGGREGATE LANDSCAPE AREAS LESS THAT 2,500 SQUARE FEET MAY COMPLY WITH THE
MWELO'S 
    APPENDIX D PRESCRIPTIVE COMPLIANCE OPTION.
A4.4 MATERIAL CONSERVATION & RESOURCE EFFICIENCY
4.406.1: JOINTS & OPENINGS.
ANNULAR SPACES AROUND PIPES, ELECTRIC CABLES, CONDUITS, OR OTHER OPENINGS IN PLATES AT EXTERIOR
WALLS SHALL BE PROTECTED AGAINST THE PASSAGE OF RODENTS BY CLOSING SUCH OPENINGS WITH CEMENT
MORTAR, CONCRETE MASONRY OR SIMILAR METHOD ACCEPTABLE TO THE ENFORCING AGENCY.
4.408.1: A MINIMUM OF 75% OR THE CONSTRUCTION WASTE GENERATED AT THE SITE IS DIVERTED TO RECYCLE OR
SALVAGE. THIS IS ACHIEVED EITHER BY USING CITY PER-CERTIFIED LANDFILLS OR IMPLEMENTATION OF A WASTE
MANAGEMENT PLAN. WASTE MANAGEMENT PLAN SHALL BE  PRE-APPROVED BY ENVIRONMENTAL SERVICES DEPT.
4.408.2 WHERE A LOCAL JURISDICTION DOES NOT HAVE A CONSTRUCTION & DEMOLITION WASTE MANAGEMENT
ORDINANCE, A CONSTRUCTION WASTE MANAGEMENT PLAN SHALL BE SUBMITTED FOR APPROVAL TO THE
ENFORCING AGENCY.
4.410.1 AN OPERATION & MAINTENANCE MANUAL SHALL BE PROVIDED TO THE BUILDING OCCUPANT OR OWNER.
A4.5 ENVIRONMENTAL QUALITY
POLLUTANT CONTROL :
4504.1  DUCT OPENINGS & OTHER RELATED AIR DISTRIBUTION COMPONENT OPENINGS SHALL BE COVERED DURING
CONSTRUCTION.
4.504.2.1 ADHESIVES, SEALANTS & CAULKS SHALL BE COMPLIANT WITH VOC & OTHER TOXIC COMPOUND LIMITS.
4.504.2.2: PAINTS, STAINS & OTHER COATINGS SHALL BE  COMPLIANT WITH VOC LIMITS.
4.5O4.2.3: ALL PAINTS & COATINGS SHALL BE COMPLIANT WITH PRODUCT WEIGHTED MIR LIMITS FOR ROC & OTHER
TOXIC COMPOUNDS.
4.504.2.4: DOCUMENTATION SHALL BE PROVIDED TO VERIFY THAT COMPLIANT VOC LIMIT FINISH MATERIALS HAVE
BEEN USED.
4.504.3: CARPET & CARPET SYSTEMS SHALL BE COMPLIANT WITH VOC LIMITS.
4.504.4: 80% OF FLOOR AREA RECEIVING RESILIENT FLOORING, SHALL COMPLY WITH THE VOC-EMISSION LIMITS
DEFINED IN THE COLLABORATIVE FOR HIGH PERFORMANCE SCHOOLS (CHPS) LOW-EMITTING MATERIALS LIST OR
BE CERTIFIED UNDER THE RESILIENT FLOOR COVERING INSTITUTE (RFCI) FLOORSCORE PROGRAMS.
4.504.5: PARTICLE BOARD, MEDIUM DENSITY FIBERBOARD (MDF), AND HARDWOOD PLYWOOD USED IN INTERIOR
FINISH SYSTEMS SHALL COMPLY WITH LOW FORMALDEHYDE EMISSIONS STANDARDS. SPECIFY THE LIMITS ON THE
PLANS IN ACCORDANCE WITH.
4.505.2: VAPOR RETARDER & CAPILLARY BREAK IS INSTALLED AT SLAB ON GRADE FOUNDATIONS.
4.505.3: MOISTURE CONTENT OF BUILDING MATERIALS USED IN WALL & FLOOR FRAMING IS CHECKED BEFORE
ENCLOSURE.
INDOOR AIR QUALITY & EXHAUST
4.506.1 ENERGY STAR COMPLIANT EXHAUST FANS WHICH TERMINATE OUTSIDE THE BUILDING ARE PROVIDED IN
EVERY BATHROOM. CONTROLLED BY A HUMIDITY CONTROL, UNLESS IT IS FUNCTIONING AS A COMPONENT OF A
WHOLE HOUSE VENTILATION SYSTEM.
ENVIRONMENTAL COMFORT
4.507.1: WHOLE HOUSE EXHAUST FANS SHALL HAVE INSULATED LOUVERS OR COVERS WHICH CLOSE WHEN THE
FAN IS OFF. COVERS OR LOUVERS SHALL HAVE A MIN. INSULATION VALUE OF R-4.2.
4.507.2: DUCT SYSTEMS ARE SIZED, DESIGNED & EQUIPMENTS IS SELECTED USING THE FOLLOWING METHODS:
1. ESTABLISH HEAT LOSS & HEAT GAIN VALUES ACCORDING TO ACCA MANUAL J OR EQUIVALENT.
2. SIZE DUCT SYSTEMS ACCORDING TO ACCA 19-D (MANUAL D) OR EQUIVALENT.
3. SELECT HEATING & COOLING EQUIPMENT ACCORDING TO ACCA 36-S (MANUAL S) OR EQUIVALENT.
INSTALLER & SPECIAL INSPECTOR QUALIFICATIONS
702.11: HVAC SYSTEM INSTALLERS ARE TRAINED & CERTIFIED IN THE PROPER INSTALLATION OF HVAC SYSTEMS.
702.2: SPECIAL INSPECTORS EMPLOYED BY THE ENFORCING AGENCY MUST BE QUALIFIED & ABLE TO
DEMONSTRATE COMPETENCE IN THE DISCIPLINE THEY ARE INSPECTING.
703.1: VERIFICATION OF COMPLIANCE WITH THIS CODE MAY INCLUDE
CONSTRUCTION DOCUMENTS, PLANS, SPECIFICATIONS, BUILDER OR INSTALLER CERTIFICATION, INSPECTION
REPORTS OR OTHER METHODS ACCEPTABLE TO THE ENFORCING AGENCY WHICH SHOW SUBSTANTIAL
CONFORMANCE.

WASTE MANAGEMENT PLAN:
CONSTRUCTION WASH-OUT WATER FROM CONCRETE, MORTAR, TILE, TAPING, AND PAINTING SHALL BE
DONE IN A PORTABLE CONTAINMENT POOL OR IN A LINED EVAPORATIVE PIT.  WASH-OUT SHALL NOT ENTER
THE STORM WATER SYSTEM.
TRASH PILES SHALL NOT BE LOCATED IN THE FRONT YARD OR VISIBLE FROM THE STREET.  TRASH PILES
SHALL NOT CONTAIN: PAINTS, SOLVENTS, GLUES, TAPING COMPOUND, FOOD PRODUCTS, OR EASILY
RECYCLE-ABLE DISCARDS SUCH AS BOTTLES, CANS, PLASTICS, OR PAPER.  REMAINING TRASH SHALL BE
LIMITED TO CONCRETE, WOOD, DRYWALL, ROOFING, AND ASSORTED METALS AND SHALL BE COVERED WITH
A WATERPROOF TARP.   TRASH SHALL BE SEPARATED AT AN APPROVED BAY AREA DISPOSAL SITE SUCH AS
GUADALUPE RECYCLING.  ALL TRASH IS TO BE QUICKLY HAULED OFF SITE.  RETAIN THE RECEIPT AND KEEP
WITH THE PERMIT DOCUMENTS, PROOF OF RECYCLE AND DISPOSAL OF THE JOB SITE TRASH WILL BE
CHECKED PERIODICALLY AND PRIOR TO FINAL INSPECTION.
OR
WEST VALLEY COLLECTION AND RECYCLING (408) 283-9250 WILL DELIVER A ROLL-OFF DEBRIS BOX AND
SORT THE TRASH OFF SITE.
EROSION CONTROL NOTES:
1.  ALL EROSION CONTROL MEASURES SHALL  BE ONSITE AND READILY ACCESSIBLE PRIOR TO
CONSTRUCTION.
2.  SWEEP OR SCRAPE UP SOILS TRACKED ONTO THE ROAD AT THE END OF EACH DAY.  DO NOT
HOSE INTO STREET, GUTTER, OR STORM DRAIN.
3.  REVEGETATE DISTURBED AREAS.  EXPOSED BARE DIRT SHALL BE COVERED WITH MULCH, JUT
NETTING OR OTHER EROSION CONTROL BLANKET. 
4.  ALL TEMPORARY STOCKPILES SHALL BE COVERED WITH 6 MIL. PLASTIC SHEETS, SUITABLY
ANCHORED.
5.  THE SITE SHALL BE MONITORED BY THE CONTRACTOR / OWNER AFTER RAIN EVENT TO VERIFY
EROSION CONTROL MEASURES ARE FUNCTIONING. 
GENERAL NOTES:
1 VERIFY LOCATION OF ALL UTILITIES AT JOB SITE.
2 SLOPE ALL FINISH GRADES A MIN. OF 5% FOR 10'-0" AWAY FROM STRUCTURE FOR DRAINAGE. IMPERVIOUS
SURFACES SHALL BE SLOPED NO LOESS THAN 2% AWAY FROM BUILDING CRC R401.3
3 ALL DWELLINGS SHALL HAVE A CONTROLLED METHOD OF WATER DISPOSAL FROM ROOFS THAT WILL
COLLECT AND DISCHARGE ROOF DRAINAGE TO THE GROUND SURFACE AT LEAST 5 FEET FROM
FOUNDATION WALLS OR TIE INTO AN APPROVED DRAINAGE SYSTEM.
4 THE FINISH GRADE AROUND THE STRUCTURE SHALL SLOPE AWAY FROM THE FOUNDATION A MINIMUM OF
5% FOR A MINIMUM DISTANCE OF 10'-0" (CBC 1804.3).
5 ON GRADED SITES, THE TOP OF ANY EXTERIOR FOUNDATION SHALL EXTEND ABOVE THE ELEVATION OF
THE STREET GUTTER AT POINT OF DISCHARGE OR THE INLET OF AN APPROVED DRAINAGE DEVICE A
MINIMUM OF 12" PLUS 2" (CRC 1808.7.4).
6 EAVE PROJECTIONS SHALL HAVE 1 HOUR FIRE-RESISTANCE RATING ON ALL EAVE PROJECTIONS THAT ARE
LESS THAN 3'-0" FROM THE PROPERTY LINE. THIS IS NOT REQUIRED FOR EAVE PROJECTIONS GREATER
THAN 3'-0" AS PRESCRIBED UNDER CRC SECTION R302 & TABLES R302.1(2).

Pre School Drop-off and Pick-up Plan 
Facility Address: 3399 CSM Drive, San Mateo CA 
General Overview:  
Western Hills Church is located on a private lot, off CSM Drive and near Parrott Drive, 
accessible through a shared access road. There is no public traffic within the Western Hills 
Church campus. There is no other ministry activities on the church campus during pre-
school drop-off and pick-up hours.  
To ensure safe, efficient and minimally disruptive traffic flow, Western Hills Church has 
developed the following drop-off and pick-up procedures. The plan is designed to protect 
child safety, reduce congestion, and ensure smooth operations for families, staff and the 
community.  
Staff Transportation and Parking 
Public Transportation is nearby. There is a bus stop on CSM drive, adjacent to the access 
road, and the College of San Mateo bus stop is nearby. Staff members can conveniently 
commute using public transportation.  
Western Hills Church has an ample amount of designated parking spots, within the church 
campus, for staff parking and family drop-off.  
Drop-off Procedures (8:00 am – 9:30 am) 
Families shall enter the Western Hills Campus, via access road from CSM Drive.   
Families will follow traffic flow plan, as indicated below, to reduce congestion and enhance 
safety. (red line)  
Families may park in the designated parking 
area and check in their child at the door.  
Families may use the designated loading zone, 
for short term parking, and check in their child 
at the door.  
Families with disabilities may use the 
designated ADA drop off area, and check in 
their child at the door.  
Staff will be present during regular drop-off 
periods to assist.  
Families are encouraged to stagger arrival 
times within the drop-off window to avoid congestion.

--- page 261 ---
Pick-up Procedures (4:30 pm – 6:00 pm) 
Families shall enter the Western Hills Campus, via access road from CSM Drive.   
Families will follow traffic flow plan, as indicated above, to reduce congestion and enhance 
safety. (red line)  
Families may park in the designated parking area or use the designed loading zone.  
Families will check-out their child, with staff, at pickup.  
Families are encouraged to pick-up at staggered times within the pick-up window to avoid 
congestion. 
Traffic Flow and Safety Measures  
1. Capacity Management 
• With a maximum capacity of 60 children, arrivals and departures are 
naturally staggered across families.  
• Fewer than 10 cars typically arrive within any 15-minute interval.  
2. Parking  
• The church campus is located on a private lot with ample parking.  
• There is no public traffic within the church campus.  
• Drop-off and pick-up should have no effect on public street traffic.  
3. Loading Zone 
• Drop-off and Pick-up must occur only in the designated parking or loading 
zones.  
4. Pedestrian Safety 
• The church campus is located on a private lot. 
• There is no public traffic within the church campus.  
• Parents must escort their children across the parking lot and into and out of 
the facility.  
• Staff supervision is provided at the pick-up and drop-off areas.  
5. Family Communication 
• Families receive clear written instructions on drop-off and pick-up 
procedures.  
• Reminders are provided regularly to ensure compliance and safety.  
 
Contingency Plan 
If traffic congestion or parking concerns arise. Western Hills will: 
• Adjust staff schedules to increase assistance during peak times.

--- page 262 ---
• Further stagger pick-up and drop off times by classrooms, if necessary.  
• Review and adjust drop-off and pick-up plan, if necessary.  
• Collaborate with the City of San Mateo to implement additional traffic management 
measures, if necessary.
